Functional summary and final compliance
- Deck: 11×3 grid centered on Stone Base; validated geometry with no overlaps.  
- Towers: Inner posts at x=±7 and outer posts at x=±8; no rigid contact with deck after scaffold removal; ring and X bracing provide rigidity and Gothic portals.  
- Upper tie-walkway: Two horizontal braces plus two diagonals across tower tops; locks spacing.  
- Suspension: After removing Blocks 41, 49, 71, 79, the only tower–deck connections are winches W1–W12; deck hangs with adjustable, static-length sag.  
- Ornaments: Powered wheels unassigned (stationary visually), torches clear of cannons (heating radius 0.3), water cannons unassigned and oriented outward along ±y.

Position adjustment note (minor, deck centerline x=−1): Block 36 is specified “west of Block 34”; in practice, attach 36 to the west face of Block 1 (Stone Base) to realize the intended x=−1 center tile without attempting to traverse through the occupied x=0 tile. Functional placement remains identical.

# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Introduction to tools I will use to build your structure step by step

I will construct your bridge exactly per your blueprint, one block or connector at a time, using the following tools. Please note: the note field on each operation is very important; I will use it to record the specific function and identity of each block or connector so we can reliably reference them later.

- start: Begins the build by placing the starter block (Block 1). Inputs:
  - init_shift [x, y, z]: initial position offset (defaults to [0, 0, 0]).
  - init_rotation [yaw, pitch, roll]: initial rotation (defaults to [0, 0, 0]).
  - note: description of the machine or Block 1’s intended role. I will use this to mark “Block 1 – Stone Base – deck datum.”
- attach_block_to: Attaches a new block to a specific face of an existing block. Allowed new_block types: Small Wooden Block, Powered Wheel, Torch, Water Cannon. Inputs:
  - base_block: the existing block’s ID.
  - face: face label to attach on. I will map blueprint phrases to faces as follows: “east of” → face "East", “west of” → "West", “north of” → "North", “south of” → "South", “top of” → "Top", and if needed “bottom of” → "Bottom".
  - new_block: the block type per blueprint.
  - note: I’ll record the exact identity (e.g., “Block 7 – Deck top row (x=+5,y=+1)”).
  If any face availability is uncertain, I will use get_block_details first.
- connect_blocks: Creates non‑volumetric connections between two faces using connectors. Allowed connectors: Brace, Winch. Inputs:
  - block_a, face_a and block_b, face_b: endpoints and faces to connect.
  - connector: Brace or Winch.
  - note: I’ll record the connection’s identity and function (e.g., “B3 – Left tower z=1 ring” or “W1 – Left inner-north top to west edge outermost”).
  If required, I can confirm faces via get_block_details to avoid proximity conflicts.
- get_block_details: Returns full details (position, rotation, face info) for a block. I’ll use this to verify coordinates, orientations, and which faces are attachable when precision matters.
- get_machine_summary: Provides the latest overall state of the machine (overview without face captions). I will use this for periodic sanity checks between steps and it is mandatory to invoke for a final check before we conclude a build stage or the entire process. I will remind you before we finalize any phase.
- shift_block: Shifts a placed block by a small offset vector [x, y, z] within [-0.5, 0.5] each, useful if an attachment overlaps or needs micro‑adjustment after placement while maintaining attachment.
- twist_block: Twists a block around its rooted face (in degrees). Helpful for orienting directional blocks (e.g., ensuring a Torch or Water Cannon points the intended direction, or adjusting a wheel’s facing).
- flip_spin: Flips spin direction of a spinning block (e.g., Powered Wheel) if needed for aesthetics or symmetry.
- remove_block: Removes a block by its ID; I will use this in Step D to delete the four temporary scaffold stubs (Blocks 41, 49, 71, 79) after all winches and upper braces are installed and tensioned.
- reset: Resets the entire machine. Not expected to be used unless we intentionally restart.

Build plan alignment with your blueprint

- I will follow your steps A through E exactly, honoring the position adjustment notes (major tower shift and the minor deck centerline note for Block 36).
- One operation per message (one new block or connector at a time). I will label each operation with the blueprint ID and use the note field to encode the identity for easy traceability.
- Orientation and faces: I’ll use the cardinal/vertical mapping given above so “east of Block N” equals attach face "East" of Block N, and so on.

Proceeding with Step A – Start and place Block 1

I will initialize the machine and place Block 1 (Stone Base) at the center of the deck grid as the reference datum. After that, I’ll proceed to Block 2 (Deck centerline x=+1, east of Block 1).

Executing: Place Block 1 – Stone Base (starter 1×1×1) – Central deck datum.
